## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt depends on position x (restoring force, possibly nonlinear), velocity v (damping, possibly nonlinear), and time t (possible external driving). Classical nonlinear oscillator equations like Duffing, van der Pol, and driven oscillators are the primary candidates.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + linear damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Driven harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (external periodic driving)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Quadratic-cubic restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric nonlinear potential)
- Nonlinear damping with cubic restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * v**3 (nonlinear damping and restoring)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x (time-modulated stiffness)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Coulomb + viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sign(v) (mixed damping types)
- General polynomial oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v + c4 * v * x**2 (general nonlinear expansion)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium, suggesting symmetric potential wells
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v represent energy dissipation or injection; sign determines damping vs. anti-damping
- Products of x**2 * v indicate amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of van der Pol-type self-excited oscillations
- Sinusoidal functions of time sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) indicate external periodic driving forces, leading to resonance phenomena
- Even powers of x (x**2) in the restoring force break spatial symmetry and indicate asymmetric potential wells
- Cubic velocity terms v**3 represent nonlinear drag forces common in fluid-coupled oscillators
- Time-dependent coefficients multiplying x suggest parametric excitation rather than direct forcing
- Absence of explicit time dependence suggests an autonomous system where energy considerations (conservative or dissipative) govern dynamics
- Combined terms like (1 - x**2)*v indicate limit cycle behavior where damping switches sign at a critical amplitude
